Once you understand what you're building, present the design in small sections (200-300 words), checking after each section whether it looks right so far.\n\n## The Process\n\n**Understanding the idea:**\n- Check out the current project state first (files, docs, recent commits)\n- Ask questions one at a time to refine the idea\n- Prefer multiple choice questions when possible, but open-ended is fine too\n- Only one question per message - if a topic needs more exploration, break it into multiple questions\n- Focus on understanding: purpose, constraints, success criteria\n\n**Exploring approaches:**\n- Propose 2-3 different approaches with trade-offs\n- Present options conversationally with your recommendation and reasoning\n- Lead with your recommended option and explain why\n\n**Presenting the design:**\n- Once you believe you understand what you're building, present the design\n- Break it into sections of 200-300 words\n- Ask after each section whether it looks right so far\n- Cover: architecture, components, data flow, error handling, testing\n- Be ready to go back and clarify if something doesn't make sense\n\n## After the Design\n\n**Documentation:**\n- Write the validated design to `docs/plans/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-design.md`\n- Use elements-of-style:writing-clearly-and-concisely skill if available\n- Commit the design document to git\n\n**Implementation (if continuing):**\n- Ask: \"Ready to set up for implementation?\"\n- Use superpowers:using-git-worktrees to create isolated workspace\n- Use superpowers:writing-plans to create detailed implementation plan\n\n## Key Principles\n\n- **One question at a time** - Don't overwhelm with multiple questions\n- **Multiple choice preferred** - Easier to answer than open-ended when possible\n- **YAGNI ruthlessly** - Remove unnecessary features from all designs\n- **Explore alternatives** - Always propose 2-3 approaches before settling\n- **Incremental validation** - Present design in sections, validate each\n- **Be flexible** - Go back and clarify when something doesn't make sense\n"

 236â†’#### `get_all_epub_files(path: str) -> List[str]`\n   237â†’Get all EPUB files in the specified directory.\n   238â†’\n   239â†’#### `get_metadata(epub_path: str) -> Dict[str, Union[str, 245â†’#### `get_chapter_markdown(epub_path: str, chapter_id: str) -> str`\n   246â†’Get chapter content in Markdown format.\n   247â†’\n   248â†’### PDF APIs\n   249â†’\n   250â†’#### `get_all_pdf_files(path: str) -> List[str]`\n   251â†’Get all PDF files in the specified directory.\n   252â†’\n   253â†’#### `get_pdf_metadata(pdf_path: str) -> Dict[str, Union[str, List[str]]]`\n   254â†’Get metadata from a PDF file.\n   255â†’\n   256â†’#### `get_pdf_toc(pdf_path: str) -> List[Tuple[str, int]]`\n   257â†’Get table of contents from a PDF file.\n   258â†’\n   259â†’#### `get_pdf_page_text(pdf_path: str, page_number: int) -> str`\n   260â†’Get plain text content from a specific page.\n   261â†’\n   262â†’#### `get_pdf_page_markdown(pdf_path: str, page_number: int) -> str`\n   263â†’Get Markdown formatted content from a specific page.\n   264â†’\n   265â†’#### `get_pdf_chapter_content(pdf_path: str, chapter_title: str) -> Tuple[str, List[int]]`\n   266â†’Get chapter content and corresponding page numbers by chapter title.\n   267â†’\n   268â†’## Dependencies\n   269â†’\n   270â†’Key dependencies include:\n   271â†’- ebooklib: EPUB file processing\n   272â†’- PyPDF2: Basic PDF processing\n   273â†’- PyMuPDF: Advanced PDF processing\n   274â†’- beautifulsoup4: HTML parsing\n   275â†’- html2text: HTML to Markdown conversion\n   276â†’- pydantic: Data validation\n   277â†’- fastmcp: MCP server framework\n   278â†’\n   279â†’## Important Notes\n   280â†’\n   281â†’1. PDF processing relies on the document's table of contents. Some features may not work if TOC is not available.\n   282â†’2. For large PDF files, it's recommended to process by page ranges to avoid loading the entire file at once.\n   283â†’3. EPUB chapter IDs must be obtained from the table of contents structure.\n   284â†’\n   285â†’## Architecture\n   286â†’\n   287â†’```\n   288â†’           â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”\n   289â†’           â”‚         Agent Layer        â”‚\n   290â†’           â”‚  -     "type": "text",
    "text": "---\n\n## Design Section 6: AI Facilitation Modes\n\nBeyond research, the AI needs to help you **think** â€” not just retrieve. Here are the modes it switches between:\n\n### Mode 1: Socratic Exploration\n**When:** You have a vague intuition (\"I feel like humans are fundamentally adaptive, but I can't articulate it\")\n\n**AI behavior:**\n- Asks one question at a time\n- Mirrors back your answer before continuing\n- Surfaces assumptions (\"What are you assuming about 'adaptive' here?\")\n- Tests consistency (\"Earlier you said X â€” how does that fit with what you just said?\")\n- Periodically summarizes what's emerged\n\n**Output:** Clearer articulation â†’ candidate for a Concept\n\n---\n\n### Mode 2: Structured Prompts\n**When:** You need to define something specific (a principle, a mechanism, a stage)\n\n**AI behavior:**\n- Presents a template with questions:\n  - \"What's the core claim?\"\n  - \"What evidence supports this?\"\n  - \"When does this NOT apply?\"\n  - \"How does this connect to [existing concept]?\"\n- Fills in as you answer\n- Flags gaps (\"You haven't addressed the nervous system piece â€” intentional?\")\n\n**Output:** Structured Concept ready for SiYuan\n\n---\n\n### Mode 3: Research Integration\n**When:** You're grounding a principle or exploring what the literature says\n\n**AI behavior:** (The process we just detailed)\n\n**Output:** Evidence-backed principle with citations\n\n---\n\n### Mode 4: Challenge/Critique\n**When:** You want to stress-test an idea\n\n**AI behavior:**\n- Plays devil's advocate\n- Asks \"What would someone who disagrees say?\"\n- Points to contradictory evidence from your library\n- Identifies edge cases\n\n**Output:** Refined, more robust principle\n\n---\n\nDoes this capture the thinking modes you need, or are there others?"

      "content": "# The Narrow Window of Awareness\n\n## Metadata\n- **Track**: 1-Human Mind\n- **Status**: developing\n- **Created**: 2025-11-29\n- **Last Updated**: 2025-11-29\n\n## Core Statement\nHumans exist in a narrow window of awareness â€” aware enough to create meaning, beliefs, and \"knowledge\" from limited sensory data, but not aware enough to see our own blind spots. This limitation is simultaneously the source of our suffering AND our unique capacity to experience meaning, beauty, love, and purpose.\n\n## Why I Believe This\n\n### From Experience\nClients often suffer not from reality itself, but from meaning they've constructed about reality without knowing they constructed it. Yet stripping away all meaning doesn't heal â€” it empties. The goal isn't \"more correct\" but \"less unnecessarily painful.\"\n\n### From Intuition\nA more advanced intelligence might see us as maximally inefficient â€” evolved enough to fight wars over skin color, not evolved enough to see the absurdity. But they'd also miss what we have: the experience of meaning itself.\n\n### From Evidence\n[TO RESEARCH: Predictive processing, meaning-making in psychology, existentialist philosophy on meaning]\n\n## The Paradox\n- Lower organisms: More efficient, less suffering, but no access to meaning\n- Higher intelligence: More correct, but meaning becomes epiphenomenal\n- Humans: Inefficient, often wrong, but uniquely positioned to EXPERIENCE meaning\n- The ignorant creation of \"false\" meaning IS meaning â€” our incorrectness is correctness\n\n## Therapeutic Implications\n1. **Not about widening awareness universally** â€” some narrowness is feature, not bug\n2. **Recognize unnecessary pain** â€” beliefs that cause suffering and CAN be revised\n3. **Allow unique contribution** â€” even when not \"the norm\"\n4. **Validate all paths** â€” mediocrity, mountain climbing, all of it matters\n5. **People matter simply because** â€” no justification needed\n\n## Open Questions\n- [ ] How do we distinguish necessary vs. unnecessary pain?\n- [ ] What makes some meaning-making \"inaccurate enough to cause suffering\"?\n- [ ] Where does neurodivergence fit â€” different window, not narrower/wider?\n- [ ] How does the nervous system interact with meaning-making?\n\n## Related Concepts\n- [[Meaning as Solution]] - meaning-making is adaptive, not pathological\n- [[Unique Personhood]] - the brain creates a singular person who matters\n- [[Unnecessary Pain]] - the clinical target (vs. unavoidable suffering)\n- [[Efficiency vs. Experience]] - the tradeoff between correctness and meaning\n\n## Research Topics to Explore\n- Predictive processing / predictive coding (Andy Clark, Karl Friston)\n- Terror Management Theory\n- Existentialist psychology (Yalom, Frankl)\n- Constructivist epistemology\n- Buddhist concept of \"useful delusion\"\n"
    }
  }

formation?\n\n### Constructivist Epistemology\n**Why**: Philosophical grounding for \"meaning is constructed, not discovered\"\n**Key authors**: Ernst von Glasersfeld, Jean Piaget, George Kelly\n**Search terms**: \"constructivism psychology\", \"personal construct theory\", \"radical constructivism\"\n**Questions to answer**:\n- What's the relationship between constructed meaning and \"truth\"?\n- How do constructivists handle the question of shared reality?\n\n### Existentialist Psychology\n**Why**: Addresses meaning-making as central human concern\n**Key authors**: Irvin Yalom, Viktor Frankl, Rollo May\n**Search terms**: \"existential psychotherapy\", \"meaning-making therapy\", \"logotherapy\"\n**Questions to answer**:\n- How does existentialism frame the \"necessity\" of meaning?\n- What's the relationship between meaning and suffering?\n\n## Priority 2: Necessary vs. Unnecessary Pain\n\n### Terror Management Theory\n**Why**: Addresses how awareness of mortality drives meaning-making (and suffering)\n**Key authors**: Sheldon Solomon, Jeff Greenberg, Tom Pyszczynski\n**Search terms**: \"terror management theory\", \"mortality salience\", \"worldview defense\"\n**Questions to answer**:\n- What pain is \"built in\" to human awareness?\n- Can awareness of death be transformed rather than defended against?\n\n### Buddhist Psychology (Secular)\n**Why**: Sophisticated framework for distinguishing suffering types\n**Key authors**: Mark Epstein, Tara Brach, Jack Kornfield\n**Search terms**: \"dukkha psychology\", \"first and second arrow\", \"Buddhist psychotherapy\"\n**Questions to answer**:\n- What's the difference between pain and suffering?\n- What's \"added\" suffering vs. unavoidable pain?\n\n## Priority 3: Neurodivergence & The Window\n\n### ADHD and Perception\n**Why**: Different attentional window â€” not narrower, differently shaped?\n**Key authors**: Russell Barkley, Edward Hallowell, Thomas Brown\n**Search terms**: \"ADHD perception\", \"ADHD attention differences\", \"ADHD and meaning-making\"\n**Questions to answer**:\n- How does ADHD change what gets \"noticed\" and therefore made into meaning?\n- Is the ADHD window wider in some dimensions, narrower in others?\n\n### Autism and Meaning-Making\n**Why**: Different pattern-detection, different meaning construction\n**Key authors**: Simon Baron-Cohen, Temple Grandin, Damian Milton\n**Search terms**: \"autism perception\", \"monotropism\", \"double empathy problem\"\n**Questions to answer**:\n- How does autistic perception differ in meaning-construction?\n- What's the relationship between pattern-detection style and worldview?\n\n## Research Process Reminder\n\nWhen using annas + ebook-mcp:\n1. Search for topic â†’ find relevant books\n2. Download top candidates\n3. Get TOC â†’ identify relevant chapters\n4. Extract chapter content â†’ pull key claims\n5. Synthesize across sources â†’ note agreements/tensions\n6. Update concept with evidence chain\n"
    }
  }
]
